  <script type="text/javascript">
    (function() {
        var contextPath = '/jira';
        var eventBuffer = [];

        function printDeprecatedMsg() {
            if (console && console.warn) {
                console.warn('DEPRECATED JS - contextPath global variable has been deprecated since 7.4.0. Use `wrm/context-path` module instead.');
            }
        }

        function sendEvent(analytics, postfix) {
            analytics.send({
                name: 'js.globals.contextPath.' + postfix
            });
        }

        function sendDeprecatedEvent(postfix) {
            try {
                var analytics = require('jira/analytics');
                if (eventBuffer.length) {
                    eventBuffer.forEach(function(value) {
                        sendEvent(analytics, value);
                    });
                    eventBuffer = [];
                }

                if (postfix) {
                    sendEvent(analytics, postfix);
                }
            } catch(ex) {
                eventBuffer.push(postfix);
                setTimeout(sendDeprecatedEvent, 1000);
            }
        }

        Object.defineProperty(window, 'contextPath', {
            get: function() {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('get');
                return contextPath;
            },
            set: function(value) {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('set');
                contextPath = value;
            }
        });
    })();

</script>

                <ul class="ops"></ul>
                <h2 class="toggle-title">Description</h2>
               </div>
               <div class="mod-content">
                <div id="description-val" class="field-ignore-highlight"> 
                 <div class="user-content-block"> 
                  <p>This ticket adds two new streaming expressions: <b>features</b> and <b>train</b></p> 
                  <p>These two functions work together to train a logistic regression model on text, from a training set stored in a SolrCloud collection.</p> 
                  <p>The syntax is as follows:</p> 
                  <div class="code panel" style="border-width: 1px;">
                   <div class="codeContent panelContent"> 
                    <pre class="code-java">train(collection1, q=<span class="code-quote">"*:*"</span>,
      features(collection1, 
               q=<span class="code-quote">"*:*"</span>,  
               field=<span class="code-quote">"body"</span>, 
               outcome=<span class="code-quote">"out_i"</span>, 
               positiveLabel=1, 
               numTerms=100),
      field=<span class="code-quote">"body"</span>,
      outcome=<span class="code-quote">"out_i"</span>,
      maxIterations=100)
</pre> 
                   </div>
                  </div> 
                  <p>The <b>features</b> function extracts the feature terms from a training set using <b>information gain</b> to score the terms. <a href="http://www.jiliang.xyz/publication/feature_selection_for_classification.pdf" class="external-link" rel="nofollow">http://www.jiliang.xyz/publication/feature_selection_for_classification.pdf</a></p> 
                  <p>The <b>train</b> function uses the extracted features to train a logistic regression model on a text field in the training set.</p> 
                  <p>For both <b>features</b> and <b>train</b> the training set is defined by a query. The doc vectors in the <b>train</b> function use tf-idf to represent the terms in the document. The idf is calculated for the specific training set, allowing multiple training sets to be stored in the same collection without polluting the idf. </p> 
                  <p>In the <b>train</b> function a batch gradient descent approach is used to iteratively train the model.</p> 
                  <p>Both the <b>features</b> and the <b>train</b> function are embedded in Solr using the AnalyticsQuery framework. So only the model is transported across the network with each iteration.</p> 
                  <p>Both the features and the models can be stored in a SolrCloud collection. Using this approach Solr can hold millions of models which can be selectively deployed. For example a model could be trained for each user, to personalize ranking and recommendations.</p> 
                  <p>Below is the final iteration of a model trained on the Enron Ham/Spam dataset. The model includes the terms and their idfs and weights as well as a classification evaluation describing the accuracy of model on the training set. </p> 
                  <div class="code panel" style="border-width: 1px;">

class=\\\"redText subText\\\" title=\\\"Joel Bernstein - 20\\/Jul\\/16 14:39\\\"\u003eedited\u003c\\/span\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eThis is part of the larger ticket \u003ca href=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/browse\\/SOLR-9258\\\" title=\\\"Optimizing, storing and deploying AI models with Streaming Expressions\\\" class=\\\"issue-link\\\" data-issue-key=\\\"SOLR-9258\\\"\u003e\u003cdel\u003eSOLR-9258\u003c\\/del\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e, which will provide more context.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eHere are some specifics about this ticket: \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eLogistic regression is a machine learning classification algorithm.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eIt\'s binary, so it\'s used to determine if something belongs to a class or not.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eWith logistic regression you train a model using a training data set. And then use that model to classify other documents. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThis ticket trains a logistic regression model on text. So it builds a model based on the terms in the documents. New documents can then be classified based on the terms in the documents.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThe terms in the document are known as \u003cb\u003efeatures\u003c\\/b\u003e. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThe first step in the process is feature selection. Which is to select the important terms from the training set that will be used to build the model. This ticket uses an algorithm called Information Gain to select the features.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThe next step is to train a model based on those features. This ticket uses Stochastic Gradient Descent to train a logistic regression model over the training set. Stochastic Gradient Descent is an iterative approach.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eBoth the features and the model can then be stored in a SolrCloud collection.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\\n\\n\\n\\n\\n\\n\\n\\n \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n                                            \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"joel.bernstein\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_15385955_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=joel.bernstein\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"joel.bernstein\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Joel Bernstein\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\\\"redText subText\\\" title=\\\"Joel Bernstein - 20\\/Jul\\/16 14:39\\\"\u003eedited\u003c\\/span\u003e                   This is part of the larger ticket   SOLR-9258  , which will provide more context. \\n\\n Here are some specifics about this ticket:  \\n\\n Logistic regression is a machine learning classification algorithm. \\n\\n It\'s binary, so it\'s used to determine if something belongs to a class or not. \\n\\n With logistic regression you train a model using a training data set. And then use that model to classify other documents.  \\n\\n This ticket trains a logistic regression model on text. So it builds a model based on the terms in the documents. New documents can then be classified based on the terms in the documents. \\n\\n The terms in the document are known as  features .  \\n\\n The first step in the process is feature selection. Which is to select the important terms from the training set that will be used to build the model. This ticket uses an algorithm called Information Gain to select the features. \\n\\n The next step is to train a model based on those features. This ticket uses Stochastic Gradient Descent to train a logistic regression model over the training set. Stochastic Gradient Descent is an iterative approach. \\n\\n Both the features and the model can then be stored in a SolrCloud collection. \\n\\n\\n\\n\\n\\n\\n\\n\\n\\n Bernstein\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_15386257_verbose subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'20\\/Jul\\/16 17:33\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2016-07-20T17:33:10+0000\'\u003e20\\/Jul\\/16 17:33\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e  \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eHere is an example of how you could use the models in a search context.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e1) Identify a training set for each user based on usage logs. This could involve what the user has viewed before, or liked. To increase the size of the training set you could use graph queries to find documents that co-occur in the same session most frequently with documents that user has viewed or liked.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e2) Optimize a model for the specific training set and store the model in a solrcloud collection. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e3) Use the model either in the re-ranker to boost documents based on the score from the model, or as part of an alerting engine to push documents the user might be interested in.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e4) Backgrounds daemons could run in Solr that would build models for users. This would result in possibly millions of models, which is fine, because the models are simply stored in a SolrCloud collection.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"joel.bernstein\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_15386257_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=joel.bernstein\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"joel.bernstein\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Joel Bernstein\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_15386257_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'20\\/Jul\\/16 17:33\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2016-07-20T17:33:10+0000\'\u003e20\\/Jul\\/16 17:33\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    Here is an example of how you could use the models in a search context. \\n\\n 1) Identify a training set for each user based on usage logs. This could involve what the user has viewed before, or liked. To increase the size of the training set you could use graph queries to find documents that co-occur in the same session most frequently with documents that user has viewed or liked. \\n\\n 2) Optimize a model for the specific training set and store the model in a solrcloud collection.  \\n\\n 3) Use the model either in the re-ranker to boost documents based on the score from the model, or as part of an alerting engine to push documents the user might be interested in. \\n\\n 4) Backgrounds daemons could run in Solr that would build models for users. \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_15392264_verbose subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'25\\/Jul\\/16 16:48\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2016-07-25T16:48:58+0000\'\u003e25\\/Jul\\/16 16:48\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e   - \u003cspan class=\\\"redText subText\\\" title=\\\"Joel Bernstein - 25\\/Jul\\/16 16:50\\\"\u003eedited\u003c\\/span\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eOk, I reviewed the TextLogisticRegressionCollector. I think we\'re going to have to change this implementation. I thought I saw an older version of this that was using the finish() method to perform the logit. But in the current version it\'s doing this in the collect method. This is going to have trouble scaling and it also requires term vectors which we don\'t want to have to use.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI think the approach to take is to collect the matching bitset in the collect() method.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThen in the finish() method the logic is:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e1) Get the top level TermsEnum\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n2) Iterate the features and seek into the terms enum\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n3) For each feature iterate the DocsEnum and compare to the matching docs bitset to build the doc vectors.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eWith this approach the DocVectors are a multi-dimension array:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003edoc0-&gt; \u003cspan class=\\\"error\\\"\u003e&#91;featureValue, featureValue, featureValue&#93;\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\ndoc1-&gt; \u003cspan class=\\\"error\\\"\u003e&#91;featureValue, featureValue, featureValue&#93;\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n...\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eWith this approach we\'ll have to hold all the docVectors in memory at once. So if you have hundreds of features and millions of records in the training set then you\'ll have a large cluster to do the work. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eWe can also add a randomized approach to this so that not every doc vector is calculated on each iteration.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\\n \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n                                            \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"joel.bernstein\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_15392264_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=joel.bernstein\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"joel.bernstein\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Joel Bernstein\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_15392264_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'25\\/Jul\\/16 16:48\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2016-07-25T16:48:58+0000\'\u003e25\\/Jul\\/16 16:48\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e   - \u003cspan class=\\\"redText subText\\\" title=\\\"Joel Bernstein - 25\\/Jul\\/16 16:50\\\"\u003eedited\u003c\\/span\u003e                   Ok, I reviewed the TextLogisticRegressionCollector. I think we\'re going to have to change this implementation. I thought I saw an older version of this that was using the finish() method to perform the logit. But in the current version it\'s doing this in the collect method. This is going to have trouble scaling and it also requires term vectors which we don\'t want to have to use. \\n\\n I think the approach to take is to collect the matching bitset in the collect() method. \\n\\n Then in the finish() method the logic is: \\n\\n 1) Get the top level TermsEnum \\n2) Iterate the features and seek into the terms enum \\n3) For each feature iterate the DocsEnum and compare to the matching docs bitset to build the doc vectors. \\n\\n With this approach the DocVectors are a multi-dimension array: \\n\\n doc0-&gt;  &#91;featureValue, featureValue, featureValue&#93;  \\ndoc1-&gt;  &#91;featureValue, featureValue, featureValue&#93;  \\n... \\n\\n With this approach we\'ll have to hold all the docVectors in memory at once. So if you have hundreds of features and millions of records in the training set then you\'ll have a large cluster to do the work.  \\n\\n We can also add a randomized approach to this so that not every doc vector is calculated on each iteration. \\n\\n\\n             \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Joel Bernstein\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_15396444_verbose subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'27\\/Jul\\/16 21:41\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2016-07-27T21:41:35+0000\'\u003e27\\/Jul\\/16 21:41\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e   - \u003cspan class=\\\"redText subText\\\" title=\\\"Joel Bernstein - 27\\/Jul\\/16 21:46\\\"\u003eedited\u003c\\/span\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eOk, here is my thinking with \u003cb\u003etrain\u003c\\/b\u003e versus \u003cb\u003etlogit\u003c\\/b\u003e\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThe \u003cb\u003etrain\u003c\\/b\u003e function would initially map directly to the TextLogitStream. We can document that \u003cb\u003etrain\u003c\\/b\u003e is a text logistic regression model trainer in the first release.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eAs we add more algorithms the \u003cb\u003etrain\u003c\\/b\u003e function will map to the \u003cb\u003eTrainStream\u003c\\/b\u003e. The TrainStream won\'t have any implementations, it will simply be a facade for different training algorithms. The TrainStream will have a parameter called \u003cb\u003ealgorithm\u003c\\/b\u003e which it will use to select the stream implementation, such as TextLogitStream. The underlying implementation will handle the parameters, all the TrainStream will do is instantiate the alogrithm and run it.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eSample syntax:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\u003cdiv class=\\\"code panel\\\" style=\\\"border-width: 1px;\\\"\u003e\u003cdiv class=\\\"codeContent panelContent\\\"\u003e\\n\u003cpre class=\\\"code-java\\\"\u003etrain(collection, \\n      features(...), \\n      algorithm=\u003cspan class=\\\"code-quote\\\"\u003e\\\"tlogit\\\"\u003c\\/span\u003e, \\n      q=\u003cspan class=\\\"code-quote\\\"\u003e\\\"*:*\\\"\u003c\\/span\u003e, ....)\\n\u003c\\/pre\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eWe can use the same facade approach for the \u003cb\u003eclassify\u003c\\/b\u003e and \u003cb\u003efeatures\u003c\\/b\u003e function. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThe documentation can provide documentation for calling title=\'27\\/Jul\\/16 21:41\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2016-07-27T21:41:35+0000\'\u003e27\\/Jul\\/16 21:41\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e   - \u003cspan class=\\\"redText subText\\\" title=\\\"Joel Bernstein - 27\\/Jul\\/16 21:46\\\"\u003eedited\u003c\\/span\u003e                   Ok, here is my thinking with  train  versus  tlogit  \\n\\n The  train  function would initially map directly to the TextLogitStream. We can document that  train  is a text logistic regression model trainer in the first release. \\n\\n As we add more algorithms the  train  function will map to the  TrainStream . The TrainStream won\'t have any implementations, it will simply be a facade for different training algorithms. The TrainStream will have a parameter called  algorithm  which it will use to select the stream implementation, such as TextLogitStream. The underlying implementation will handle the parameters, all the TrainStream will do is instantiate the alogrithm and run it. \\n\\n Sample syntax: \\n  \\n train(collection, \\n      features(...), \\n      algorithm= \\\"tlogit\\\" , \\n      q= \\\"*:*\\\" , ....)\\n \\n  \\n\\n We can use the same facade approach for the  classify  and  features  function.  \\n\\n The documentation can provide documentation for calling  train  with different algorithms.  \\n\\n I like this approach because it provides three very easy to understand functions: train, classify and features \\n\\n It also stops the explosion of functions that would occur when we have multiple classify, train and features algorithms. \\n\\n\\n\\n\\n\\n\\n\\n\\n             \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n
